<div id="review_270643956" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/270643956" />
    <a title="Katie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7586081-katie"><img alt="Katie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1483317195p2/7586081.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/270643956?book_show_action=true">Jan 31, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Katie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Katie" href="/user/show/7586081-katie">Katie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7586081-katie?shelf=ya">ya</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer270643956" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4457804217147960012">This book started out interestingly, with an interesting character voice and concept, but it did not hold together throughout, and by the end I was fed up and wishing to be done with it. The main character has something that is like Asperger’s but not actually Asperger’s, which makes it convenient for the author to pick his symptoms, I guess. He hears music in his head, has a special interest in religion, has trouble understanding people, and sometimes refers to himself and people he’s addressin</span>
  <span id="freeText4457804217147960012" style="display:none">This book started out interestingly, with an interesting character voice and concept, but it did not hold together throughout, and by the end I was fed up and wishing to be done with it. The main character has something that is like Asperger’s but not actually Asperger’s, which makes it convenient for the author to pick his symptoms, I guess. He hears music in his head, has a special interest in religion, has trouble understanding people, and sometimes refers to himself and people he’s addressing in the third person. <br /><br />One thing I noticed was that he speaks in a precise manner, and sometimes the other characters speak in the same way, even though that manner of speech isn’t in character for them. It was like the style bled through, and the author couldn’t differentiate the characters. I know Wendell is the evil, nasty character, but I don’t believe he would basically <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[tell Marcelo he was going to rape Jasmine <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> and I didn’t believe that Marcelo would want to be friends with that guy in the first place. Marcelo’s connection with Jasmine was undeveloped, and it was unbelievable that he would decide to <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[move to Vermont to be with her <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> at the time he did. The central mystery, if you can call it that, was fairly dull and obvious.<br /><br /> My least favorite thing, though, is the lack of connection Marcelo seemed to feel to those things that were at first presented as key parts of his character. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[He stops hearing the music, but no sense of loss is shown; instead, he has a muted reaction that basically amounts to a shrug. He stops his “remembering” and starts forgetting his knowledge of religion. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> He basically loses a lot of the “autistic-like” qualities the author gave him in the first place and is fine with joining the “real world.” This is not a satisfying resolution to the plot. The mental music turns out to be more of a metaphor for making moral choices than an actual important part of the plot. Speaking of moral choices, the whole philosophical discussions of morality toward the end did not ring true at all. I never got the impression the choice Marcelo made was even difficult for him, and that made it hard to take seriously all the musing. It felt trite; the plot and characters of this book are too thin to support a believable conclusion on such topics. </span>
  <a data-text-id="4457804217147960012" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_78617804" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/78617804" />
    <a title="Hallie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1145657-hallie"><img alt="Hallie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1244842998p2/1145657.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/78617804?book_show_action=true">Nov 22, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Hallie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Hallie" href="/user/show/1145657-hallie">Hallie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audio CD 9780739379899" href="/book/show/6454727-marcelo-in-the-real-world">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1145657-hallie?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1145657-hallie?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer78617804" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1520748365019636379">Still digesting this a bit, but my general feeling is that there was a bit too much going on, though much of it was wonderful. The combination of a regular coming-of-age story with a 'Asperger's is the closest to a description of my condition' one with a romance with a legal-mystery with a spiritual coming-of-age was a lot for one book, and I thought it left some of the elements which were resolved wonderfully in one sphere very much less so in another. The spiritual and the regular coming-of-ag</span>
  <span id="freeText1520748365019636379" style="display:none">Still digesting this a bit, but my general feeling is that there was a bit too much going on, though much of it was wonderful. The combination of a regular coming-of-age story with a 'Asperger's is the closest to a description of my condition' one with a romance with a legal-mystery with a spiritual coming-of-age was a lot for one book, and I thought it left some of the elements which were resolved wonderfully in one sphere very much less so in another. The spiritual and the regular coming-of-age elements worked beautifully together for example, but Marcelo's slower than 'normal' development and slower than 'normal' ability to figure things out left me more unhappy with the romantic resolution. Granted, Marcelo hadn't <i>had</i> to rise to the challenge to that degree ever before, and his learning curve might well be expected to be quicker than average, but still. The guy who a few weeks before was unable to decide whether to help his 'friend' Wendell (a stinker if there ever was one!), who was obviously (to the reader) intent on setting up a date-rape, a few weeks later being ready to decide on the plan for the rest of his life, involving a romantic commitment to a *much* more mature-seeming girl... not so sure. <br /><br />That said, I loved the whole treatment of figuring out what the moral/ethical course of action is when it's complicated. And Aurora was wonderful, though I kind of wished there hadn't been such a divide between the moral judgment of his parents, although in fairness, there was one adult male on the side of the angels for the most part, to balance it out. I was also a bit less than taken with Jasmin's dad, who seemed to take the crusty, earthy Vermont close-to-the-land thing to amazingly crude heights!<br /><br />The book obviously made me think though, given all that rambling.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1520748365019636379" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_297085725" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/297085725" />
    <a title="Kwoomac" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2076898-kwoomac"><img alt="Kwoomac" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1333998762p2/2076898.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/297085725?book_show_action=true">Mar 19, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kwoomac" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kwoomac" href="/user/show/2076898-kwoomac">Kwoomac</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2076898-kwoomac?shelf=2013">2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2076898-kwoomac?shelf=contemporary-lit">contemporary-lit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2076898-kwoomac?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2076898-kwoomac?shelf=strong-female-protag">strong-female-protag</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2076898-kwoomac?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2076898-kwoomac?shelf=coming-of-age">coming-of-age</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2076898-kwoomac?shelf=audio">audio</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2076898-kwoomac?shelf=social-commentary">social-commentary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2076898-kwoomac?shelf=there-s-a-message">there-s-a-message</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2076898-kwoomac?shelf=autism">autism</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer297085725" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12574249437992332700">A problem I have when either reading an ebook (my autocorrect wants to change this to snook!) or listening to an audio book is that I have no real sense of where I am in the story. Is this conflict being introduced halfway through the story or is it near the end? It makes a difference. For me this is important info so I can try to figure out where the author is going, if he is going somewhere. With Marcelo, I kept thinking, okay now it's near the end but it never was. Okay, at some point it was </span>
  <span id="freeText12574249437992332700" style="display:none">A problem I have when either reading an ebook (my autocorrect wants to change this to snook!) or listening to an audio book is that I have no real sense of where I am in the story. Is this conflict being introduced halfway through the story or is it near the end? It makes a difference. For me this is important info so I can try to figure out where the author is going, if he is going somewhere. With Marcelo, I kept thinking, okay now it's near the end but it never was. Okay, at some point it was because the book did end, but I guess this would mean I thought the book was too long. Maybe I'd feel different if I read it. <br /><br />I did like the book. I just didn't love it, I'm not quite sure why. I guess I didn't really believe that Marcelo was a real 17 year old boy. I couldn't help feeling like I was being hit over the head with a lesson. Marcelo (in the real world) must learn how to navigate this real world when what he experiences doesn't quite match up with what he has learned about life at home and at his private school. Again, I did like the book. I really liked the character Jasmine, I thought she was a strong female character. I also like Jerry Garcia, but that may be because every single time I heard his name I thought about Cherry Garcia, my favorite! And I loved the discussions Marcelo had with the rabbi. I want a rabbi like that to help me sort out all the big questions in life. I thought the scenes involving Jasmine's father talking crudely about fucking were a little jarring, and thus unnecessary in this otherwise sweet book. <br /><br />This book did make me want to be a better person. More thoughtful, forgiving, tolerant. Probably not going to happen but it's a nice thought.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12574249437992332700" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('knrPb2Nhby+FPkOQVFp/8WE/d0kW+DUFBbQUipdAvPfHd10QmWhEgVCveSDHf4gb4ly0lV55hyrQUk2q1JM1SQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('FstRqrIco40XgJq+d0KSywMyPvjpu4aoyRyKOeL7T25DxsPVSBWII8IRoA7kZ2UhgFH9JKE6NIcc+tMZoSjG0A==')})
  }

For his part in the conspiracy, Gantos was sentenced to serve up to six years in prison.In Hole in My Life, this prizewinning author of over thirty books for young people confronts the period of struggle and confinement that marked the end of his own youth. <span id="freeTextContainer16647169590479940004">Francisco X. Stork was born in Mexico. He moved to El Paso Texas with his adoptive father and mother when he was nine. He attended Spring Hill College, Harvard University and Columbia Law School. He worked as an attorney for thirty-three years before retiring in 2015. He is married and has two grown children and four beautiful grandkids. He loves to discover new books and authors. His favorite boo</span>
  <span id="freeText16647169590479940004" style="display:none">Francisco X. Stork was born in Mexico. He moved to El Paso Texas with his adoptive father and mother when he was nine. He attended Spring Hill College, Harvard University and Columbia Law School. He worked as an attorney for thirty-three years before retiring in 2015. He is married and has two grown children and four beautiful grandkids. He loves to discover new books and authors. His favorite books are those where the author's soul touches his. He does not read reviews to his books so you should feel free to write whatever you want. Also, he is genuinely interested in learning about books and life from his friends on this site. He would love it if you find his books worthy to be read, but that's not why he wants to be your friend.<br /></span>
